ARTICLE 1 
THE CONTRACT DOCUMENTS 
 
§1.1 The Contract Documents consist of this Agreement, Conditions of the Contract (General, 
Supplemental and other Conditions, if applicable), Amendments, Drawings, Specifications, 
Addenda issued prior to execution of this Agreement, other documents listed in this Agreement, 
and Modifications including Change Orders issued after execution of this Agreement and any 
amendments thereto. These form the Contract, and are as fully a part of the Contract as if 
attached to this Agreement or repeated herein. The Contract represents the entire and integrated 
agreement between the parties hereto and supersedes prior negotiations, representations or 
agreements, either written or oral. An enumeration of the Contract Documents, other than 
Modifications, appears in Article 14 and includes all exhibits and schedules attached hereto and 
made part hereof (collectively, the “Contract Documents”).

ARTICLE 2    
THE WORK OF THIS CONTRACT 
 
§2.1  The Contractor shall fully execute the Work described in the Contract Documents, except 
to the extent specifically indicated in the Contract Documents where work is defined to be the 
responsibility of others. 
 
§2.2 Marketing Office and Model Units: Contractor acknowledges that Owner requires a 
marketing office and model units of the residential units contemplated for the Project. Contractor 
shall cooperate with Owner to identify acceptable locations for said required marketing office 
and model units and provide as part of its scope of services such coordination, sequencing of 
work, application with, and permitting by Governmental Authorities and the like so as to allow 
the Owner to have access to completed model units to market the Project to the public and 
prospective residents (including a temporary certificate of occupancy or other permits needed to 
authorize the lawful use of the completed model units for marketing and sales by Owner or its 
agents as contemplated hereby). The Owner shall maintain and control the marketing office upon 
turnover, but the Contractor shall assist the Owner in establishing, constructing, permitting and 
opening the on-site marketing office including extending required utilities, landscaping, and 
interior finish-out, and be responsible for assisting in keeping it operational, including but not 
limited to access, parking, facilitating signage, utility service, etc. The Contractor shall ensure 
that the Owner has lawful access to and use of the marketing office for the purpose of marketing 
and sales by Owner or its agents to the public and prospective residents as contemplated herein 
by no later than nine (9) months prior to Substantial Completion of the entire Project.  The 
Contractor shall ensure that the Owner has lawful access to and use of the model units for the 
purpose of marketing and sales by Owner or its agents to the public and prospective residents as 
contemplated herein by no later than three (3) months prior to Substantial Completion of the 
entire Project.  The Contractor shall use reasonable efforts to accomplish such sequencing, 
coordination, and services, and shall incorporate such work into the Project Schedule so both 
parties can avoid creating additional costs and impacts to the Schedule resulting from such work.  
 
ARTICLE 3 
DATE OF COMMENCEMENT AND SUBSTANTIAL COMPLETION 
 
§ 3.1 The
 date of commencement of the Work shall be seven  (7) days after a formal Notice to 
Proceed is issued by the Owner.  
 
§ 3.2 The Contract Time shall be measured from the Commencement Date set forth in the Notice 
to Proceed. 
 
§ 3.2.1 The Owner, in its sole discretion, may issue a limited notice to proceed for a limited 
component of the Work.  The Commencement Date from which the Contract Time shall be 
measured shall not be established by a limited notice to proceed.  There shall be no additional 
fee, markups, or General Conditions costs or General Requirements costs because of or related to 
the issuance of a limited notice to proceed. 
 
§ 3.3 Milestone Dates; Substantial Completion; Liquidated Damages:  The
  Contractor shall 
achieve Substantial Completion of the entire Work not later than Four Hundred Seventy-Three 
(473) calendar days from the Commencement Date. The Contractor understands and agrees that 
time is of the essence in completing the Work required under the Contract Documents, and that 


===== PAGE 2 =====
3 
 
Initialed ____/____ 
 
the Owner will suffer substantial hardship and incur substantial damages if the Work is not 
completed on time, or if the Contractor fails to achieve Substantial Completion on or before the 
scheduled Substantial Completion date set forth above, as such date may be modified under the 
Contract Documents. The parties agree that such damages are difficult or impossible to 
determine with certainty, and therefore have in good faith estimated as fair compensation (and 
not as a penalty) the liquidated damages set forth below. If the Contractor fails to achieve 
Substantial Completion on or before the scheduled date set forth above, as such date may be 
modified in accordance with the Contract Documents, the Contractor shall pay the Owner 
liquidated damages, as fair compensation (and not as a penalty), in accordance with the 
following : 
 
 $2,000  per day for each day beyond the Substantial Completion date 
 
The assessment of liquidated damages shall be paid per calendar day until Substantial 
Completion shall be achieved. Liquidated damages shall be assessed cumulatively in accordance 
with the Contract Documents. Contractor hereby expressly agrees to waive its right to challenge 
the enforceability of this provision, and agrees that the liquidated damages amounts represent a 
reasonable measurement of damages, and not as a penalty, that Owner will sustain in the event of 
late performance.  These liquidated damages are in lieu of Owner’s actual direct or consequential 
damages or losses as a result of Contractor's failure to achieve Substantial Completion of the 
Work.  
 
The Owner may deduct liquidated damages from any amounts due or to become due Contractor, 
or the Owner may require Contractor to pay any liquidated damages which exceed amounts due 
or to become due to Contractor within ten (10) days after Owner’s written request. Contractor 
waives and Owner is not required to comply with any other notice provisions in order to assess 
and/or deduct liquidated damages.  Owner may assess and/or deduct the amount of liquidated 
damages by withholding the amount of the liquidated damages from the payment due to 
Contractor on any pay application(s) and paying that amount to itself. 
 
The Contractor shall complete all final Punch List work such that Final Completion shall be 
achieved within thirty (30) days (or later, upon notice of Contractor to Owner, and approval by 
Owner in writing, for specific items where thirty (30) days is not practical) of Substantial 
Completion or receipt of the final Punch List, whichever is later.   
 
The Contractor will give monthly schedule updates to Owner and a firm commitment sixty (60) 
days prior to the anticipated Substantial Completion date. 
 
§3.4 If the Contractor believes that the Work will not be substantially complete on or before the 
Da
te of Substantial Completion, the Contractor shall have the right to remedy such anticipated 
delay, through accele ration and overtime work in order to prevent the imposition of liquidated 
damages as provided herein. Such costs shall be the responsibility of the Contractor  within the 
GMP.  Such costs shall be a Cost of the Work unless they arise or result in any way from the 
negligence or responsibility of the Contractor or its Subcontractors or suppliers  or arise or result 
in any way from any cause beyond the control of the Owner.  
 
§3.5 Early Completion Bonus: If
  the Work is Substantially Complete prior to the Date of 
Substantial Completion, the Contractor shall be paid an early completion bonus of $1,000 /day 
per each calendar day for a maximum of thirty (30) days. The Contractor must provide a

ARTICLE 4 
CONTRACT SUM 
 
§ 4.1  The Owner shall pay the Contractor the Contract Sum in current funds for the Contractor's 
performance of the Contract. The Contract Sum is the Cost of the Work as defined in this 
Agreement plus the Contractor's Fee. 
 
§ 4.2  Contractor's Fee: For
  completion of the Work required by the Contract Documents, the 
Contractor’s Fee is the lump sum amount of Seven Hundred Fifty Six Thousand One Hundred 
Thirty-Nine  ($756,139).  For changes in the Work, the Contractor’s Fee shall be 2.75% of the 
net increase/decrease of a change order plus additions for Subcontractor Default Insurance 
(1.2%) Contractor Controlled Insurance program (2.5%),  P&P Bond(s) (1%) and Builder’s Risk 
(0.36%). 
 
§ 4.3  Guaranteed Maximum Price: The sum of the Cost of the Work and the Contractor's Fee is 
guaranteed by the Contractor not to exceed Twenty-Eight Million Two Hundred Fifty Two 
Thousand One Hundred  Dollars ($28,252,100) subject to additions and deductions by Change 
Order as provided in the Contract Documents. Such maximum sum is referred to in the Contract 
Documents as the Guaranteed Maximum Price or GMP. Costs which would cause the 
Guaranteed Maximum Price to be exceeded shall be the responsibility of  the Contractor, and 
Contractor shall pay such amounts without reimbursement by the Owner. 
 
To the extent that the Cost of the Work and the Contractor’s Fee is less than the Guaranteed 
Maximum Price, the Contractor shall be entitled to share such  “savings” realized by the Owner 
in connection with the Project as follows:  
 
--first $100,000 of savings shall be distributed 30% to the Contractor and 70% to Owner; 
 
--second $100,000 of savings shall be distributed 25% to the Contractor and 75% to Owner;  
 
--third $100,000 of savings shall be distributed 20% to the Contractor and 80% to Owner; 
 
--fourth $100,000 of savings shall be distributed 15% to the Contractor and 85% to Owner; 
 
--fifth $100,000 of savings shall be distributed 10% to the Contractor and 90% to Owner.  
 
All remaining savings shall be to and for the benefit of the Owner. The Contractor’s share of the 
savings as broken down above shall be capped at $100,000. 
 
§ 4.3.1  Contractor’s Contingency. The Owner and Contractor agree that the Guaranteed 
Maximum Price includes a separate contingency (“Contractor’s Contingency”) in the amount of 
Four Hundred Ninety-Nine Thousand Nine Hundred Fifty-Two Dollars ($499,952).   The 
Contractor’s Contingency is available for the Contractor’s use solely to cover costs reimbursable 
as a Cost of the Work, Subject to Article 6, but not included in a Change Order.  The 
Contractor’s Contingency shall be used only to pay for Costs of the Work not reasonably 
anticipatable by the Contractor on or before the date of this Agreement and which are not 


===== PAGE 4 =====
5 
 
Initialed ____/____ 
 
otherwise included or covered by other line items in the Schedule of Values or the basis of a 
Change Order under the Contract Documents.  By way of example only, the Owner and 
Contractor contemplate that the Contractor’s Contingency may be used to cover Costs of the 
Work arising out of the following: (a) refinement of details of the design within the scope and 
standards of quality and quantities on which the Guaranteed Maximum Price of the Project was 
based; (b) corrective Work not due to the fault or negligence of the Contractor and not able to be 
back-charged to Subcontractors (or to the Contractor for any self-performed trade work), 
provided Contractor has exhausted all reasonable means to obtain correction of same from any 
responsible Subcontractors; (c) nonperformance by Subcontractors that cannot otherwise 
reasonably be recovered; (d) costs arising during construction that could not be adequately 
anticipated by the Contractor at the time of preparing the Guaranteed Maximum Price; and (e) 
unintended gaps or omissions in the buy-out of the Work or unintended buy-out overruns.  The 
Contractor acknowledges and agrees that the Owner has a legitimate desire to keep the Contract 
sum below the Guaranteed Maximum Price to the fullest extent reasonably practicable.  
Therefore, the Contractor shall use the Contractor’s Contingency in good faith and prudently.  In 
no event shall the Contractor’s Contingency be used for any of the following:  (a) any work 
necessary due to Contractor’s negligence or breach of its obligations under the Construction 
Documents; (b) the Contractor’s Fee;; (d) any Cost of the Work recovered from or through (i) 
any Subcontractor, supplier or other person or entity performing any Work, or (ii) bond, 
insurance or other security pertaining to the performance of the Work; or (f) any item that does 
not constitute a Cost of the Work.  Contingency Use Authorization forms are contained in 
Exhibit L.  Contractor shall submit to the Owner and Architect a Contingency Use Authorization 
form for each instance in which Contractor proposes to use all or any part of the Contractor’s 
Contingency in excess of Thirty-five Thousand Dollars ($35,000).  Notwithstanding the previous 
sentence, regardless of amount, any request by Contractor to use Contractor’s Contingency to 
increase the General Conditions line item of the Schedule of Values  must be submitted on a 
Contingency Use Authorization form for Owner’s review and approval.  Contractor shall fully 
describe the amount and basis for the proposed use of the Contractor’s Contingency in the 
Contingency Use Authorization form and shall provide documentation support for proposed 
expenditures to the reasonable satisfaction of the Owner.  Contractor acknowledges and agrees 
that it may not use all or any part of the Contractor’s Contingency for General Conditions costs 
any amount without the prior submission to Owner of a Contingency Use Authorization form 
and Owner’s written approval for such payment in Owner’s reasonable discretion.  Contractor 
further acknowledges and agrees that it may not use all or any part of the Contractor’s 
Contingency in excess of the threshold amount stated above without the prior submission of a 
Contingency Use Authorization form and Owner’s written approval for such payment, which 
approval shall not be unreasonably withheld.  Any use of the Contractor’s Contingency without 
the prior submission of a Contingency Use Authorization form and Owner’s written approval is 
not valid and shall be returned to the Owner immediately.  In addition to the Contingency Use 
Authorization forms, Contractor shall provide the Owner with a monthly written report 
describing the Contractor’s use of the Contractor’s Contingency.  Each month the Contractor’s 
use of the Contractor’s Contingency shall be reconciled with the Owner during the pay 
application review process.  Contractor acknowledges and agrees that Owner has discretion to 
reject any proposed or actual use of the Contractor’s Contingency to the extent the proposed use 
does not satisfy the requirements stated in the Contract.

§ 4.8 To the extent that the Drawings and Speci fi

§ 4.9  When used in the Contract Documents, the letters “GMP” shall be deemed to refer to the 
Guaranteed Maximum Price. The parties will work in good faith to consider value engineering 
options to facilitate quality improvements and Work for the Project and shall complete the 
evaluation of Value Engineering items within sixty (60) days of the Commencement Date. As 
such, a value engineering log will be created and maintained by the Contractor and shared with 
the Owner. When Value Engineering items are fully evaluated and accepted, a Change Order 
shall be executed by the Owner and the Contractor.   
  
ARTICLE 5 
COSTS TO BE REIMBURSED  
 
§ 5.1 Cost of the Work 
The term “Cost of the Work” shall mean costs necessarily incurred by the Contractor in the 
proper performance of the Work. Such costs shall be at rates not higher than the standard paid at 
the place of the Project except with prior, written consent of the Owner. The Cost of the Work 
shall include only the items set forth in this Article 5 per rates set forth on Exhibit E. 
 


===== PAGE 6 =====
7 
 
Initialed ____/____ 
 
§ 5.1.1 General Conditions Amount: The General Conditions Amount quantified below is the 
amount paid to reimburse the Contractor for all General Conditions costs. Notwithstanding 
anything to the contrary in the Contract Documents, the total cost to the Owner for all General 
Conditions costs for the Work shall in no event exceed One Million Four Hundred Seventy 
Thousand  Seventy Seven Dollars ($1,470,077.00) inclusive of all applicable taxes (“General 
Conditions Amount”). without Owner approval which shall not be unreasonably withheld.  Costs 
of General Conditions items that would either cause the Guaranteed Maximum Price to be 
exceeded or that constitute amounts not approved by Owner shall be paid by the Contractor 
without reimbursement from the Owner.  
 
§ 5.2 Labor Costs 
§ 5.2.1 Wages of construction workers directly employed by the Contractor to perform the 
construction of the Work at the site or, with the Owner's approval, at off-site workshops which 
will be billed as a Cost of the Work in accordance with Reimbursable General Conditions & 
Overall Schedule per Exhibit E. 
 
§ 5.2.2 Wages or salaries of the Contractor's supervisory and administrative personnel when 
working on the Project with the Owner's approval per Exhibit E.   
 
 
§ 5.2.3 Wages and salaries of the Contractor's supervisory or administrative personnel engaged, 
at factories, workshops or on the road, in expediting the production or transportation of materials 
or equipment required for the Work, but only for that portion of their time required for the Work. 
 
§ 5.2.4 Costs paid or incurred by the Contractor for taxes, insurance, contributions, assessments 
and benefits required by law or collective bargaining agreements and, for personnel not covered 
by such agreements, customary benefits such as sick leave, medical and health benefits, holidays, 
vacations and pensions, provided such costs are based on wages and salaries included in the Cost 
of the Work under this Article 5 and Exhibit E.  
 
§ 5.2.5  The Cost of the Work shall be credited with all rebates, trade discounts, credits on taxes 
or credits realized on cash deposits or insurance premiums, and Contractor shall take such steps 
as are reasonably necessary and appropriate to obtain such discounts, rebates and credits which 
will be applied for the benefit of Owner.   
 
§ 5.3 Subcontract Costs 
§ 5.3.1 Payments made by the Contractor to Subcontractors in accordance with the requirements 
of the subcontracts. 
 
§ 5.4 Costs of Materials and Equipment Incorporated in the Completed Construction 
§ 5.4.1 Costs, including transportation and storage, of materials and equipment incorporated or to 
be incorporated in the completed construction. 
 
§ 5.4.2 Costs of materials described in the preceding Article 5.4.1 in excess of those actually 
installed to allow for reasonable waste and spoilage. Unused excess materials, if any, shall 
become the Owner's property at the completion of the Work or, at the Owner's option, shall be 
sold by the Contractor. Any amounts realized from such sales shall be credited to the Owner as a 
deduction from the Cost of the Work.

§ 5.5 Costs of Other Materials and Equipment, Temporary Facilities and Related Items 
§ 5.5.1 Costs, including transportation and storage, installation, maintenance, dismantling and 
removal of materials, supplies, temporary facilities, machinery, equipment, and hand tools not 
customarily owned by construction workers, that are provided by the Contractor at the site and 
fully consumed in the performance of the Work; and cost (less salvage value) of such items if not 
fully consumed, whether sold to others or retained by the Contractor. Cost for items previously 
used by the Contractor shall mean fair market value. 
 
§ 5.5.2 Rental charges for temporary facilities, machinery, equipment, and hand tools not 
customarily owned by construction workers that are provided by the Contractor at the site, 
whether rented from the Contractor or others, and costs of transportation, installation, minor 
repairs and replacements, dismantling and removal thereof. Rates and quantities of equipment 
rented shall be subject to the Owner's prior approval.  Rental rates of Contractor-owned 
equipment are set forth in Exhibit E hereto. 
 
§ 5.5.3 Costs of removal of debris from the site. 
 
§ 5.5.4 Costs of document reproductions, facsimile transmissions and long-distance telephone 
calls, postage and parcel delivery charges, telephone service at the site and reasonable petty cash 
expenses of the site office. 
 
§ 5.5.5 That portion of the reasonable expenses of the Contractor's personnel incurred while 
traveling in discharge of duties directly connected with the Work, excluding travel to and from 
the Project location and the Contractor’s office, provided that such expenses are authorized in 
advance by the Owner. 
 
§ 5.5.6 Costs of materials and equipment suitably stored off the site at a mutually acceptable 
location, if approved in advance by the Owner in writing. 
 
§ 5.6 Miscellaneous Costs 
§ 5.6.1 That portion of insurance and bond premiums that can be directly attributed to this 
Contract as approved by Owner and not otherwise excluded by Article 6 or the Contract 
Documents.  Contractor shall provide Owner documents (i.e. – establishing the enrolled 
subcontract value for the CCIP and SDI programs, etc.) to prove that the insurance and bond 
premiums charged to this Contract is for insurance and bonds directly attributed to this Contract 
and no others to the Owner’s reasonable satisfaction.  
 
§ 5.6.1.1 Unless otherwise noted herein, refunds of premiums received by Contractor from an 
insurer or surety shall be credited or paid to Owner, as applicable. 
 
§ 5.6.2 Sales, use or similar taxes imposed by a governmental authority that are related to the 
Work. 
 
§ 5.6.3 Fees and assessments for the building permit and for other permits, licenses and 
inspections for which the Contractor is required by the Contract Documents to pay. 
 
§ 5.6.4 Fees of laboratories for tests required by the Contract Documents, except those related to 
defective or nonconforming Work for which reimbursement is excluded by the Contract 
Documents, and which do not fall within the scope of Article 5.7.3.

approval shall not be unreasonably withheld. 
 
§ 5.6.9 Expenses incurred in accordance with the Contractor's standard personnel policy for 
relocation and temporary living allowances of personnel required for the Work, if approved by 
the Owner. 
 
§ 5.7 Other Costs and Emergencies 
§ 5.7.1 Other costs incurred in the performance of the Work if and to the extent approved in 
advance in writing by the Owner. 
 
§ 5.7.2 Costs due to emergencies incurred in taking action to prevent threatened damage, injury 
or loss in case of an emergency of an immediate, acute, and imminent nature affecting the 
physical safety of persons and property, only as provided in the General Conditions. 
 
§ 5.7.3 Costs of repairing or correcting damaged or nonconforming Work executed by the 
Contractor, Subcontractors or suppliers, provided that such damaged or nonconforming Work 
was not caused by negligence or failure to fulfill a specific responsibility of the Contractor and 
only to the extent that the cost of repair or correction is not recoverable by the Contractor from 
insurance, sureties, Subcontractors or suppliers (of any tier).

ARTICLE 7 
DISCOUNTS, REBATES AND REFUNDS 
 
§ 7.1 Cash discounts obtained on payments made by the Contractor shall accrue to the Owner if 
(1) before making the payment, the Contractor included them in an Application for Payment and 
received payment therefor from the Owner, or (2) the Owner has deposited funds with the 
Contractor with which to make payments; otherwise, cash discounts shall accrue to the 
Contractor. Trade discounts, rebates, refunds and amounts received from sales of surplus 
materials and equipment shall accrue to the Owner, and the Contractor shall make provisions so 
that they can be secured and paid. 
 
§ 7.2 Amounts that accrue to the Owner in accordance with the provisions of Section 7.1 shall be 
credited to the Owner as a deduction from the Cost of the Work. 
 
ARTICLE 8 
SUBCONTRACTS AND OTHER AGREEMENTS 
 
§ 8.1 Those portions of the Work that the Contractor does not customarily perform with the 
Contractor's own personnel shall be performed under subcontracts or by other appropriate 
agreements with the Contractor. The Owner may designate specific persons or entities from 
whom the Contractor shall obtain bids. The Contractor shall obtain bids from Subcontractors and 
from suppliers of materials or equipment fabricated especially for the Work and shall deliver 
such bids to the Architect. The Owner shall then determine, with the advice of the Contractor and 
the Architect, which bids will be accepted. Owner agrees to use its best efforts to assist 
Contractor in resolving disputes and performance issues with Subcontractors or suppliers who 


===== PAGE 10 =====
11 
 
Initialed ____/____ 
 
have been expressly specified in the Contract Documents or who provide proprietary systems for 
which there is not a reasonable alternative.  
 
§ 8.2 If a specific bidder among those whose bids are delivered by the Contractor to the Architect 
(1) is recommended to the Owner by the Contractor; (2) is qualified to perform that portion of 
the Work; and (3) has submitted a bid that conforms to the requirements of the Contract 
Documents without reservations or exceptions, but the Owner requires that another bid be 
accepted, then the Contractor may require that a Change Order be issued to adjust the 
Guaranteed Maximum Price by the difference between the bid of the person or entity 
recommended to the Owner by the Contractor and the amount of the subcontract or other 
agreement actually signed with the person or entity designated by the Owner. 
 
§ 8.3 Subcontracts or other agreements shall conform to the applicable payment provisions of 
this Agreement and the Contract Documents generally, and shall not be awarded on the basis of 
cost plus a fee without the prior written consent of the Owner. 
 
§ 8.4 The Contractor shall provide the Owner with copies of all subcontracts within thirty (30) 
days of execution thereof. 
 
ARTICLE 9 
ACCOUNTING RECORDS 
 
The Contractor shall keep full and detailed accounts and exercise such controls as may be 
necessary for proper financial management under the Contract Documents, and the accounting 
and control systems shall be reasonably satisfactory to the Owner. The Owner and the Owner's 
accountants shall be afforded reasonable access to, and shall be permitted to audit and copy upon 
reasonable advance notice, the Contractor's records, books, correspondence, instructions, 
drawings, receipts, subcontracts, purchase orders, vouchers, memoranda and other data relating 
to this Contract, and the Contractor shall preserve these for a period of three (3) years after final 
payment, or for such longer period as may be required by law.  Contractor shall keep complete 
all proposals received or prepared by Contractor for changed Work and permit Owner to inspect 
and copy all proposals so that Owner may fully understand the cost basis of each proposed 
change.  A like Accounting Records provision shall be included in all subcontracts (of any tier) 
so that Owner may inspect Subcontractor’s books and records.

General Conditions line item of the Schedule of Values be adjusted or changed without the 
written approval of the Owner.  This Schedule of Values, unless objected to by the Architect or 
Owner, shall be used as a basis for reviewing the Contractor's Applications for Payment.

the

actually been completed; or (2) the percentage obtained by dividing (a) the expense that has 
actually been incurred by the Contractor on account of that portion of the Work for which the 
Contractor has made or intends to make actual payment prior to the next Application for 
Payment by (b) the share of the Guaranteed Maximum Price allocated to that portion of the Work 
in the Schedule of Values.

Completion of the Work by the Contractor, the Contractor shall be paid a sum sufficient to 
increase the total payments to the Contractor to 100% of the Cost of the Work and Fees, but less 
an amount equal to 200% of the costs of the Work for incomplete Work or Punch List Work.  
However, in no event will the retainage be reduced lower than the amount required by the 
Lender in the Construction Loan Agreement. In the event of any inconsistency between this 
retainage clause and the Construction Loan Agreement, the Construction Loan Agreement shall 
govern.

ARTICLE 1   GENERAL PROVISIONS 
 
§ 1.1 BASIC DEFINITIONS 
 
§ 1.1.1 THE CONTRACT DOCUMENTS 
The Contract Documents consist of the Agreement between Owner and Contractor 
(hereinafter the Agreement), these General Conditions of the Contract (hereinafter the 
General Conditions), Supplemental and other Conditions (if applicable), Amendments, 
Drawings, Specifications, Addenda issued prior to execution of the Agreement, other 
documents listed in the Agreement, and Modifications, including Change Orders, issued 
after execution of the Agreement, and any amendments thereto.  
 
A Modification is (1) a written amendment to the Contract signed by both parties, (2) a 
Change Order, (3) a Construction Change Directive, (4) a written order for a minor 
change in the Work issued by the Owner, or (5) an ASI (Architect’s Supplemental 
Instruction) when signed by both the Owner and the Architect.   
 
Unless specifically enumerated in the Agreement, the Contract Documents do not include 
other documents such as bidding requirements (advertisement or invitation to bid, 


===== PAGE 22 =====
 
Initials ___/___ 
 
Instructions to Bidders, sample forms, the Contractor's bid or portions of Addenda 
relating to bidding requirements) or geotechnical reports.  If geotechnical reports are 
provided to the Contractor, they are provided for reference and information only and are 
not design documents. 
 
§ 1.1.2 THE CONTRACT 
The Contract Documents form the Contract for Construction. The Contract represents the 
entire and integrated agreement between the parties hereto and supersedes prior 
negotiations, representations or agreements, either written or oral. The Contract may be 
amended or modified only by a Modification. The Contract Documents shall not be 
construed to create a contractual relationship of any kind (1) between the Architect and 
Contractor, (2) between the Owner and a Subcontractor or Sub-subcontractor (at any 
tier), except as set forth in §§ 5.3 and 5.4, (3) between the Owner and Architect or (4) 
between any persons or entities other than the Owner and Contractor. The Architect shall, 
however, be entitled to performance and enforcement of obligations under the Contract 
intended to facilitate performance of the Architect's duties. 
 
§ 1.1.3 THE WORK 
The term "Work" means the construction and services required by the Contract 
Documents, whether completed or partially completed, and includes all other labor, 
materials, equipment and services provided or to be provided by the Contractor to fulfill 
the Contractor's obligations. The Work may constitute the whole or a part of the Project. 
 
§ 1.1.4 THE PROJECT 
“The Project” means the construction project identified in the Agreement and on the first 
page of these General Conditions and the Work performed thereat or required to be 
performed under the Contract Documents. 
 
§ 1.1.5 OTHER DEFINITIONS 
 
§1.1.5.1  The term “Agreement” shall mean the Guaranteed Maximum Price Construction 
Agreement Between the Owner and the General Contractor. References to “this 
Agreement” or “the Agreement” shall refer to this instrument, which is one of the 
Contract Documents.  
§1.1.5.2  The term “Allowances” shall mean the allowable amount for the Cost of the 
Work (as defined herein) for specific items/portions of the Work, which items/portions 
and related amounts are identified and described in Section 4.6 of the Agreement and the 
applicable Exhibit thereto.  
§1.1.5.3  The term “Architect” shall mean the architect identified in the Agreement and 
shall be deemed to include authorized representatives. 
§1.1.5.4  The term “Certificate of Insurance” shall mean a certificate issued by an 
insurance company or representative that confirms the existence of the insurance required 
of Contractor for the Project, the limits of coverage, its expiration date and additional 
insureds. 


===== PAGE 23 =====
 
Initials ___/___ 
 
 
§1.1.5.5  The term “Claim” shall mean a demand or assertion by one of the parties 
seeking, as a matter of right,  adjustment or interpretation of Contract terms, payment of 
money, extension of time or other relief with respect to the terms of the Contract. The 
term "Claim" also includes other disputes and matters in question between the Owner and 
Contractor arising out of or relating to the Contract. A demand for money or services by a 
third party is not a Claim.     
§1.1.5.6  The term “Contract Schedule” shall mean the schedule for the performance and 
completion of the Work attached Exhibit C to the Agreement.  The Contract Schedule 
sets forth the progress and milestones of the Work and the agreed upon date for 
Substantial Completion of the Project.   
§1.1.5.7  The term “Contract Time” shall mean the period of time allotted in the Contract 
Schedule attached hereto as Exhibit C within which Contractor shall achieve Substantial 
Completion of the Work.

including Section 4.3 of the Agreement.

expression “reasonably inferable” and similar terms in the Contract Documents shall be

prepared by the Architect; however, the Contractor shall have a duty to notify Owner and

§ 1.2 CORRELATION AND INTENT OF THE CONTRACT DOCUMENTS 
§ 1.2.1 The intent of the Contract Documents is to include all items necessary for the 
proper execution and completion of the Work by the Contractor. The Contract 
Documents are complementary, and what is required by one shall be as binding as if 
required by all; performance by the Contractor shall be required only to the extent 
consistent with the Contract Documents and reasonably inferable from them as being 
necessary to produce the indicated results. 


===== PAGE 26 =====
 
Initials ___/___ 
 
 
§ 1.2.2 Organization of the Specifications into divisions, sections and articles, and 
arrangement of Drawings shall not control the Contractor in dividing the Work among 
Subcontractors or in establishing the extent of Work to be performed by any trade. 
 
§ 1.2.3 Unless otherwise stated in the Contract Documents, words which have well-
known technical or construction industry meanings are used in the Contract Documents 
in accordance with such recognized meanings. 
 
§ 1.2.4 All work mentioned or indicated in the Contract Documents shall be performed 
by the Contractor as part of this Contract unless the Contract Documents specifically 
indicate that such work is to be done by others. 
 
§ 1.2.5 The Contractor and all Subcontractors shall refer to all of the Drawings, including 
those showing primarily the work of the mechanical, electrical and other specialized 
trades, and all of the Sections of the Specifications, and shall perform all work reasonably 
inferable therefrom as being necessary to produce the indicated results. 
 
§ 1.2.6 All indications of notations which apply to one of a number of similar situations, 
materials or processes shall be deemed to apply to all such situations, materials or 
processes wherever they appear in the Work, except where a contrary result is clearly 
indicated by the Contract Documents.   
 
§ 1.2.7 It shall be the responsibility of the Contractor to identify, quantify and present a 
report to the Owner identifying items of omission and/or incomplete scope which it 
discovers in the Contract Documents.  Contractor shall endeavor to complete its review 
within forty-five (45) days of the issuance of the construction set documents to determine 
whether there are any items of omission and/or incomplete scope in the Contract 
Documents and so report to the Owner.   
 
§ 1.2.8 Where codes, standards, requirements and publications of public and private 
bodies are referred to in the Specifications, Drawings or other Contract Documents, 
references shall be understood to be the latest revision as of the date of the issuance of 
such documents, except where otherwise indicated. 
 
§ 1.2.9 Where no explicit quality or standards for materials or workmanship are 
established for work, such work is to be of good quality for the intended use and 
consistent with the quality of the surrounding work and of the construction of the Project 
generally. 
 
§ 1.2.10 All manufactured articles, materials, and equipment shall be applied, installed, 
connected, erected, used, cleaned and conditioned in accordance with the manufacturer’s 
written or printed directions and instructions unless otherwise indicated in the Contract 
Documents.

§ 1.2.11 The Mechanical and Electrical Drawings are not intended to show the exact 
physical locations or configurations of work within the design locations and space.  Such 
work shall be installed to clear all obstructions, permit proper clearances for the work of

substitutions may be made unless accepted prior to execution of the Contract and listed in

§ 1.3 CAPITALIZATION 
§ 1.3.1 Terms capitalized in these General Conditions include those which are (1) 
specifically defined, (2) the titles of numbered articles or (3) the titles of other documents 
published by the American Institute of Architects. 
 
§ 1.4 INTERPRETATION 
§ 1.4.1 In the interest of brevity the Contract Documents frequently omit modifying 
words such as "all" and "any" and articles such as "the" and "an," but the fact that a 
modifier or an article is absent from one statement and appears in another is not intended 
to affect the interpretation of either statement.

the Owner or Contractor or both do not sign all the Contract Documents, the Architect 
shall identify such unsigned Documents upon request.

form, prepared by the Architect and the Architect's consultants are Instruments of Service

may retain one record set. Neither the Contractor nor any Subcontractor, Sub-
subcontractor or material or equipment supplier shall own or claim a copyright in the 
Drawings, Specifications and other documents prepared by the Architect or the 
Architect's consultants, and unless otherwise indicated, the Architect and the Architect's 
consultants shall be deemed the authors of them and will retain all common law, statutory 
and other reserved rights, in addition to the copyrights. All copies of Instruments of 
Service, except the Contractor's record set, shall be returned or suitably accounted for to 
the Architect, on request, upon completion of the Work. The Drawings, Specifications 
and other documents prepared by the Architect and the Architect's consultants, and copies 
thereof furnished to the Contractor, are for use solely with respect to this Project. They 
are not to be used by the Contractor or any Subcontractor, Sub-subcontractor or material 
or equipment supplier on other projects or for additions to this Project outside the scope 
of the Work without the specific written consent of the Owner, Architect and the 
Architect's consultants. The Contractor, Subcontractors, Sub-subcontractors and material 
or equipment suppliers are authorized to use and reproduce applicable portions of the 
Drawings, Specifications and other documents prepared by the Architect and the

ARTICLE 2   OWNER 
§ 2.1 GENERAL 
§ 2.1.1 The Owner is the person or entity identified as such in the Agreement and is 
referred to throughout the Contract Documents as if singular in number. The Owner shall 
designate in writing a representative who shall have express authority to bind the Owner 
with respect to all matters requiring the Owner's approval or authorization. Except as 
otherwise provided in § 4.2.1, the Architect does not have such authority to bind the 
Owner.  The term "Owner" means the Owner or the Owner's authorized representative(s). 
 
§ 2.2 INFORMATION AND SERVICES REQUIRED OF THE OWNER 
§ 2.2.1 The Owner shall, at the written request of the Contractor, prior to commencement 
of the Work and thereafter, furnish to the Contractor reasonable evidence that financial 
arrangements have been made to fulfill the Owner's obligations under the Contract. 
Furnishing of such evidence shall be a condition precedent to commencement or 
continuation of the Work.  
 
§ 2.2.2 Except for permits and fees, including those required under § 3.7.1, which are the 
responsibility of the Contractor under the Contract Documents, the Owner shall secure 
and pay for necessary plan check approvals and easements. 
 
§ 2.2.3 The Owner shall furnish site surveys describing physical characteristics, legal 
limitations and utility locations for the site of the Project, and a legal description of the 
site. The Contractor shall be entitled to rely on the accuracy of such survey information 
furnished by the Owner but shall exercise proper precautions relating to the safe 
performance of the Work. 
 
§ 2.2.4 Information or services required of the Owner by the Contract Documents shall be 
furnished by the Owner with reasonable promptness after receipt from the Contractor of a 
written request for such information or services. Any other information or services 
relevant to the Contractor's performance of the Work under the Owner's control shall be 


===== PAGE 30 =====
Initials ___/___ 
 
furnished by the Owner after receipt from the Contractor of a written request for such 
information or services. 
§ 2.2.5 Unless otherwise provided in the Contract Documents, the Contractor will be
furnished, free of charge, one set of Contract Drawings and Project Manuals.
§ 2.3 OWNER'S RIGHT TO STOP THE WORK
§ 2.3.1 If the Contractor fails to correct Work which is not in accordance with the
requirements of the Contract Documents as required by § 12.2 or persistently fails to
carry out Work in accordance with the Contract Documents, the Owner may issue a
written order to the Contractor to stop the Work, or any portion thereof, until the cause
for such order has been eliminated; however, the right of the Owner to stop the Work
shall not give rise to a duty on the part of the Owner to exercise this right for the benefit
of the Contractor or any other person or entity.  This right shall be in addition to, and not
in restriction of, the Owner’s rights as otherwise set forth in  the Contract Documents.
The Owner’s right to stop the Work shall not relieve Contractor of any of its
responsibilities or obligations under or pursuant to the Contract Documents.
§ 2.4 OWNER'S RIGHT TO CARRY OUT THE WORK
§ 2.4.1 If the Contractor defaults or neglects to carry out the Work in accordance with the
Contract Documents and fails within a seven-day period after receipt of written notice
from the Owner to commence and continue correction of such default or neglect with
diligence and promptness, the Owner may, without prejudice to other remedies the
Owner may have against the Contractor, correct such deficiencies.   In the event that the
Owner, in its sole discretion, determines that such deficiency is considered a “life safety
event,” hazard, emergency or for any other reason needs to be corrected immediately, the
Owner may correct such deficiency immediately, without giving written or verbal notice
to the Contractor.  In such cases, an appropriate Change Order shall be issued deducting
from payments then or thereafter due the Contractor the costs of correcting such
deficiencies, including Owner's expenses and compensation for the Architect's additional
services made necessary by such default, neglect or failure. If payments then or thereafter
due the Contractor are not sufficient to cover such amounts, the Contractor shall pay the
difference to the Owner.

referred to throughout the Contract Documents as if singular in number. The term
"Contractor" means the Contractor or the Contractor's authorized representative.
§ 3.1.2 The Contractor shall perform the Work in accordance with the Contract
Documents.
§ 3.1.3 The Contractor shall not be relieved of obligations to perform the Work in
accordance with the Contract Documents either by activities or duties of the Architect in

the Architect's administration of the Contract, or by tests, inspections or approvals 
required or performed by persons other than the Contractor.  
 
§ 3.1.4 The Contractor accepts the relationship of trust and confidence established 
between the Contractor and the Owner by the Agreement and the Conditions of the 
Agreement. Contractor covenants with the Owner to furnish its best skill and judgment, 
to cooperate with the Architect in furthering the interests of the Owner, to furnish 
efficient business administration and superintendence, to use its best efforts to furnish at 
all times an adequate supply of workmen and materials, and to perform the Work in 
accordance with the Contract Documents. 
 
§ 3.2 REVIEW OF CONTRACT DOCUMENTS AND FIELD CONDITIONS 
BY CONTRACTOR 
 
§ 3.2.1 Since the Contract Documents are complementary, in order to facilitate 
coordination and construction and not in the role of a design professional, engineer, peer 
reviewer, or for the express purpose of finding errors and omission in the Drawings and 
Contract Documents, before starting the Work and each portion of the Work, the 
Contractor shall carefully study and compare the various Drawings and other Contract 
Documents relative to that portion of the Work, as well as the information furnished by 
the Owner pursuant to § 2.2.3, shall take field measurements of any existing conditions 
related to that portion of the Work and shall observe any conditions at the site affecting it. 
The Contractor shall immediately report to the Owner and the Architect, in writing, any 
error, inconsistency, omission or problem with any construction feasibility it discovers. 
Any necessary change shall be ordered in accordance with Article 7, subject to the 
requirements of the provisions of the Contract Documents. If the Contractor proceeds 
with work without such notice to the Architect and the Owner, having discovered such 
errors, inconsistencies or problems with construction feasibility, or if by such reasonable 
study of the site and the Contract Documents he should have discovered such, the 
Contractor shall bear all costs that would have been avoided by not performing the 
obligations in this article.   
 
§ 3.2.2 If the Contractor believes that additional cost or time is involved because of 
clarifications or instructions issued by the Architect in response to the Contractor's 
notices or requests for information pursuant to § 3.2.1, the Contractor shall make Claims 
as provided in § 4.3.6 and § 4.3.7. If the Contractor fails to perform the obligations of § 
3.2.1, the Contractor shall pay such costs and damages to the Owner as would have been 
avoided if the Contractor had performed such obligations.  
 
§ 3.2.3 The Contractor shall give the Architect and the Owner timely written notice of 
any additional design drawings, specifications, or instructions which are required to 
define the Work in greater detail, or to permit the proper progress of the Work. 
 
§ 3.2.4 The Contractor shall not proceed with any Work not clearly and consistently 
defined in the Contract Documents, but shall request additional drawings or instructions 
from the Architect and Owner as provided in subparagraph 3.2.3. If the Contractor

 
proceeds with such Work without obtaining further drawings or instructions, he shall 
correct Work incorrectly done at his own expense and waives any rights to recovery. 
 
§ 3.3 SUPERVISION AND CONSTRUCTION PROCEDURES 
§ 3.3.1 The Contractor shall supervise and direct the Work, using the Contractor's best 
skill and attention. The Contractor shall be solely responsible for and have control over 
construction means, methods, techniques, sequences and procedures and for coordinating 
all portions of the Work under the Contract, unless the Contract Documents give other 
specific instructions concerning these matters. Except as otherwise provided herein, the 
Contractor shall be responsible for the methods, techniques, sequences or procedures 
employed by him (including all loss, damage, liability or cost of correcting defective 
work arising therefrom) if the same are not required by the Contract Documents. 
   
§ 3.3.1.1 Where the Contract Documents refer to particular construction means, methods, 
techniques, sequences or procedures or indicate or imply that such are to be used in the 
Work, the Contractor shall review the same carefully and shall advise the Owner and the 
Architect in writing if he determines that the same may not be safely and suitably 
employed on the Work, specifying the actual methods, techniques, sequences and 
procedures in the notice. The Contractor shall be responsible for any loss, liability, cost 
or damage if it fails to use diligence in timely reviewing the prescribed or implied means, 
methods, techniques or procedures, or proceeds with such means, methods, techniques or 
procedures without providing the required notice to the Architect or Owner. The 
Contractor shall not proceed with the Work using such means, methods, techniques, 
sequences or procedures without further written instructions from the Architect.  
 
§ 3.3.2 The Contractor shall be responsible to the Owner for acts and omissions of the 
Contractor's employees, Subcontractors and their agents and employees, and all other 
persons or entities performing or supplying the Work for or on behalf of the Contractor or 
any of its Subcontractors and for any damages, losses, costs and expenses, including, but 
not limited to, attorneys’ fees, resulting from such acts and omissions.  The Contractor 
shall use standards of care required of a reasonably prudent contractor or as otherwise 
called for in the Contract Documents to coordinate and supervise the Work performed by 
Subcontractors so that the Work is carried out without conflict between trades and so that 
no trade, at any time, causes delay to the general progress of the Work. The Contractor 
and all Subcontractors shall at all times afford each trade, any separate contractor, or the 
Owner every reasonable opportunity for the installation of work and storage of materials. 
 
§ 3.3.3 The Contractor shall be responsible for inspection of portions of Work already 
performed to determine that such portions are in proper condition to receive subsequent 
Work. The Contractor shall be responsible for scheduling and coordinating all tests and 
inspections of the Work, and shall be fully responsible for advising the Owner and the 
Architect, and any other entity, of the date and time of such testing or inspection, if their 
presence or observance is required at such testing or inspection. The Contractor shall be 
fully responsible for providing the testing or inspection entity with copies of or access to 
the most up-to-date and complete Contract Documents specifying the type or quality of 
the portion of the Work being tested.

 
 
§ 3.3.4 The Contractor shall arrange for and attend job meetings with the Architect and 
the Owner’s representative and such other persons as the Owner may from time to time 
wish to have present. The Contractor shall designate a representative in the form of a

Registered Land Surveyor, who shall establish the exterior line and required elevations of 
all buildings, site work, and structures included in the Work. The Registered Engineer or 
Land Surveyor shall certify as to the actual location of the constructed facilities in 
relations to property lines, buildings lines, easements, and other restrictive boundaries.  
Such obligation under this section shall not include an ALTA survey or special survey 
requirements stipulated by any governmental body.  
 
§ 3.4 LABOR AND MATERIALS 
§ 3.4.1 Unless otherwise provided in the Contract Documents, the Contractor shall 
provide and pay for labor, materials, equipment, tools, construction equipment and 
machinery, water, heat, utilities, transportation, and other facilities and services necessary 
for proper execution and completion of the Work, whether temporary or permanent and 
whether or not incorporated or to be incorporated in the Work. The word “provide” shall 
mean furnish and install complete, including connections, unless otherwise specified. 
 
§ 3.4.2 The Contractor may make substitutions only with the express written consent of 
the Owner, after evaluation by the Architect and in accordance with a Change Order. 
 
§ 3.4.3 The Contractor shall enforce strict discipline and good order among the 
Contractor's employees and other persons carrying out the Contract. The Contractor shall 
not permit employment of unfit persons or persons not skilled in tasks assigned to them, 
and shall replace persons who cause disruption to the progress of the Work at no cost to 
the Owner. 
 
§ 3.4.4 The Contractor shall also use commercially reasonable efforts to minimize the 
likelihood of any strike, work stoppage, or other labor disturbance, except for area-wide 
or national strikes or other labor actions not directed at Contractor or within Contractor’s 
reasonable control.

.1 If the Work is to be performed by trade unions, the Contractor shall make all

§ 3.5 WARRANTY 
§ 3.5.1 The Contractor warrants to the Owner that materials and equipment furnished 
under the Contract will be of good quality and new unless otherwise required or 
permitted by the Contract Documents, that the Work will be free from defects not 
inherent in the quality required or permitted, and that the Work will conform to the 
requirements of the Contract Documents. Work not conforming to these requirements, 
including substitutions not properly approved and authorized, shall be considered 
defective.  The Contractor's warranty excludes remedy for damage or defect caused by 
abuse, modifications not executed by the Contractor, improper or insufficient 
maintenance, improper operation, or normal wear and tear and normal usage. If required 
by the Architect, the Contractor shall furnish satisfactory evidence as to the kind and 
quality of materials and equipment. 
 
§ 3.5.2 Contractor shall be responsible for determining that all materials and labor 
furnished by Contractor or its Subcontractors (of any tier), suppliers or materialmen for 
the Work meet all requirements of the Contract Documents. The Architect may require 
the Contractor to produce reasonable evidence that a material meets such requirements, 
such as certified reports of passed test by qualified experts, or other evidence which in the 
opinion of the Architect, would lead to a reasonable certainty that any material used, or 
proposed to be used, in the Work meets the requirements of the Contract Documents. All 
such data shall be furnished at the Contractor’s expense as a cost of the Work. 
 
§ 3.5.3 In all cases in which a manufacturer’s name, trade name or other proprietary 
designation is used in connection with materials or articles to be furnished under the 
Contract, whether or not the phrase “or equal” is used after such name, the Contractor 
shall furnish to the extent possible the product of the named manufacturer(s) without 
substitution, unless a written request for a substitute has been submitted by the Contractor 
and approved in writing by the Architect and Owner as provided in Subparagraph 3.5.4. 


===== PAGE 35 =====
 
Initials ___/___ 
 
The Owner makes no warranty as to availability, availability at a particular time, or 
obtainable price for any material or articles to be furnished under this Contract by 
Contractor and it is the Contractor’s sole responsibility to procure all such Contractor 
provided materials and articles in a timely manner so as not to delay the Work.  
 
§ 3.5.4 If the Contractor proposes to use a material which, while suitable for the intended 
use, deviates in any way from the detailed requirements of the Contract Documents, he 
shall inform the Architect and the Owner in writing of the nature of such deviation at the 
time the material is submitted for approval, and shall request written approval of the 
deviation from the requirements of the Contract Documents.   
 
§ 3.5.5  In requesting approval of deviations or substitutions, the Contractor shall 
provide, upon request, evidence leading to a reasonable certainty that the proposed 
substitution or deviation (separate and distinct from Value Engineering) will provide a 
quality of result at least equal to that otherwise attainable. If, in the opinion of the 
Architect or the Owner, the evidence presented by the Contractor does not provide a 
sufficient basis for certainty, the Architect or the Owner may reject such substitution or 
deviation without further investigation.  In the event a deviation or substitution is 
approved which requires deviations in related Work, such as partitions, foundations, 
wiring, ductwork, piping, etc., the Contractor shall be responsible at its expense for 
preparing and submitting new drawings and detailing to the Architect for approval and 
for performing any additional work and supplying any additional materials required as a 
result of such substitution or deviation, at no cost to Owner and without delay to the 
Project, unless the Owner and/or Architect is the sole cause of the deviation and/or 
substitution. Approval of a substitution request does not in any way relieve the Contractor 
from liability for failure to comply with the Contract Documents. Architect, similar to 
Architect Supplemental Instructions, has a responsibility to review and properly 
incorporate Architect/Owner-requested Substitutions into the design.  
 
§ 3.5.6 The Contract Documents are intended to produce a Project of consistent character 
and quality of design. All components of any building including visible items of 
mechanical and electrical equipment have been selected to have a coordinated design in 
relation to the overall appearance of the building. The Architect shall judge the design 
and appearance of proposed Contractor substitutes on the basis of their suitability in 
relation to the overall design of the Project, as well as for their intrinsic merits. The 
Architect will not approve as equal to materials specified any Contractor proposed 
substitutes which, in its opinion, would be out of character, obtrusive, or otherwise 
inconsistent with the overall character or quality of design of the Project. In order to 
permit a coordinated design of color and finishes the Contractor shall, if required by the 
Architect, furnish the substituted material in any color, finish texture, or pattern which 
would have been available from the manufacturer originally specified, regardless of 
whether this is a custom color or profile in the opinion of the substitute supplier, at no 
additional cost to the Owner.

documents and specification information pertaining to the allowance, and 
prior to commencing work associated with the allowances.

§ 3.10 CONTRACTOR'S CONSTRUCTION SCHEDULES 
§ 3.10.1 The Contractor shall include an exhibit as part of the Contract Documents 
detailing the Critical Path Method (CPM) Contract Schedule, clearly delineating the 
Project’s critical path. This schedule shall be referred to as the “Contract Schedule” and 
may only be changed or altered by a mutually agreed upon Change Order. The Contract 
Schedule shall not exceed time limits current under the Contract Documents, shall be 
revised at appropriate intervals as required by the conditions of the Work and Project, 
shall be related to the entire Project to the extent required by the Contract Documents, 
and shall provide for expeditious and practicable execution of the Work. 
 
§ 3.10.2 The Contractor shall prepare and keep current, for the Architect's approval, a 
schedule of submittals which is coordinated with the Contractor's Construction Schedule, 
including to ensure that the critical path milestones are met, and allows the Architect 
reasonable time to review submittals. The Contractor shall maintain a Project record set 
of all submittals.  The Contractor shall regularly update the submittal schedule with 
revised submittal dates and material procurement dates that reflect the current progress of 
he Work.  Each updated submittal schedule shall be submitted to the Owner and the 
Architect for approval. If the Contractor fails to submit a submittal schedule or any 
necessary updates, the Contractor shall not be entitled to any increase in Contract Sum or 
extension of Contract Time based on the time required for review of submittals.    
 
§ 3.10.3 With each Payment Application, the Contractor shall submit an updated Contract 
Schedule for approval by the Owner and Architect. The Contractor shall perform the 
Work in accordance with the current Contract Schedule approved by the Owner and 
Architect.

§ 3.10.4 The Contract Schedule shall be based on an orderly progression of the Work, 
allowing adequate time for each operation, and leading to Substantial Completion by the 
date(s) established in the Agreement. The Contractor must coordinate its work with the 
work of other third-party contractors. The Contract Schedule will be reviewed by the

to extend the time for completion as provided in Subparagraph 4.3.7, the calendar dates 
in the Contract Schedule shall be adjusted accordingly to retain their same relationship to 
the adjusted date of Substantial Completion, and the dollar value of work to be completed 
as the first of each month shall be adjusted pro-rata. 
 
§ 3.10.6 The Contractor shall furnish sufficient forces, plant and equipment and shall 
work such hours, including night shifts and lawful overtime operations as may be 
necessary to ensure the prosecution of the work in accordance with the Contract 
Schedule. If, in the opinion of the Owner, the contractor falls behind schedule, the 
Contractor must take such steps as may be necessary to improve his progress, and must 
submit his plans demonstrating the manner in which the desired rate of progress may be 
regained. It shall be the responsibility of the Contractor to maintain his schedule so as not 
to delay the progress of the Work or the scheduled work of other persons. If Contractor 
delays the progress of the Work, in order to regain the time lost and to maintain the 
Contract Schedule, it shall be the responsibility of the Contractor to increase the number 
of shifts, days of Work, and/or to the extent permitted by law, to institute or increase 
overtime operations, all without additional cost to the Owner in excess of the GMP. 
 
§ 3.10.7 In order to expedite the completion of the Work, the Owner, in his sole 
discretion, may direct the Contractor to increase the number of shifts, days of work, 
and/or perform overtime operations or to take such other measures as he deems necessary 
to expedite construction. Such instruction shall be in writing and signed by the Owner. 
The Contractor, however, shall not be entitled to any additional costs unless the need for 
such direction was not attributable to the actions, omissions, delays or other fault of the 
Contractor. In such an event, the Owner shall pay the Contractor the additional cost as 
mutually agreed upon in writing. If the Contractor is behind schedule due to his own 
actions, omissions, delays or other fault on its part and the Owner directs the Contractor 
to work additional shifts, overtime, expedite deliveries, supplement its forces or purchase 
additional materials or equipment in order to bring his work up to schedule, all additional 
cost in excess of the GMP shall be borne by the Contractor.  
 
§ 3.10.8  Progress of “work by Owner” shall not modify or relieve the Contractor of his 
obligation to maintain his adherence to the Contract Schedule and completion date,

§ 3.11 DOCUMENTS AND SAMPLES AT THE SITE 
§ 3.11.1 The Contractor shall maintain at the site for the Owner one record copy of the

order and marked currently to record field changes and selections made during 
construction, and one record copy of approved Shop Drawings, Product Data, Samples 
and similar required submittals. These shall be available to the Architect and the Owner 
during the Project, and shall be delivered to the Architect for submittal to the Owner upon 
completion of the Work. 
 
§ 3.11.1.1 Recorded changes shall, at a minimum, include architectural and structural 
changes; plumbing, heating, ventilating and air conditioning changes; electrical changes; 
and changes to site Work including grades and utilities.

Daily Log throughout the duration of the Project.  These shall be available to the 
Architect and the Owner during the Project, and shall be delivered to the Architect for 
submittal to the Owner upon completion of the Work. 
 
§ 3.12 SHOP DRAWINGS, PRODUCT DATA AND SAMPLES 
§ 3.12.1 Shop Drawings are drawings, diagrams, schedules and other data specially 
prepared for the Work by the Contractor or a Subcontractor, Sub-subcontractor, 
manufacturer, supplier or distributor to illustrate some portion of the Work. 
 
§ 3.12.1.1 Within two (2) weeks after being awarded the Contract, Contractor is required 
to submit for the Owner and Architect’s approval a Schedule for the submission of all 
shop drawings, product data and samples required on the Project. 
 
§ 3.12.1.2 All submissions involving visible components of the Project, including 
roofing, siding, brick, paints, etc., shall be submitted within ninety (90) days of the 
Notice to Proceed as a finish materials package.   
 
§ 3.12.2 Product Data are illustrations, standard schedules, performance charts, 
instructions, brochures, diagrams and other information furnished by the Contractor to 
illustrate materials or equipment for some portion of the Work. 
 


===== PAGE 41 =====
 
Initials ___/___ 
 
§ 3.12.3 Samples are physical examples which illustrate materials, equipment or 
workmanship and establish standards by which the Work will be judged. 
 
§ 3.12.4 The purpose of Shop Drawings, Product Data, Samples and similar submittals is 
to demonstrate for those portions of the Work for which submittals are required by the 
Contract Documents the way by which the Contractor proposes to conform to the 
information given and the design concept expressed in the Contract Documents. Review 
by the Architect is subject to the limitations of § 4.2.7. Informational submittals upon 
which the Architect is not expected to take responsive action may be so identified in the 
Contract Documents. Submittals which are not required by the Contract Documents may 
be returned by the Architect without action. 
 
§ 3.12.5 The Contractor shall review for compliance with the Contract Documents, 
approve and submit to the Architect Shop Drawings, Product Data, Samples and similar 
submittals required by the Contract Documents with reasonable promptness and in such 
sequence as to cause no delay in the Work or in the activities of the Owner or of separate 
contractors. Submittals which are not marked as reviewed for compliance with the 
Contract Documents and approved by the Contractor may be returned by the Architect 
without action. 
 
§ 3.12.6  By approving and submitting Shop Drawings, Product Data, and Samples, the 
Contractor thereby represents that he has determined and verified in accordance with the 
applicable standard of care of a reasonably prudent contractor all dimensions, quantities, 
field dimensions, relations to existing structures and work, coordination with work to be 
installed later, coordination with information on previously accepted Shop Drawings, 
Product Data, or Samples and verification of compliance with all the requirements of the 
Contract Documents. The accuracy of all such information, provided it remains 
unchanged by the Architect, is the responsibility of the Contractor; said review does not 
remove or mitigate Architect’s obligation to review, approve, or coordinate with Design.   
 
§ 3.12.7 The Contractor shall perform no portion of the Work for which the Contract 
Documents require submittal and review of Shop Drawings, Product Data, Samples or 
similar submittals until the respective submittal has been approved by the Architect. 
 
§ 3.12.8 The Work shall be in accordance with approved submittals except that the 
Contractor shall not be relieved of responsibility for deviations from requirements of the 
Contract Documents by the Architect's approval of Shop Drawings, Product Data, 
Samples or similar submittals unless the Contractor has specifically informed the 
Architect in writing of such deviation at the time of submittal and (1) the Architect has 
given written approval to the specific deviation as a minor change in the Work, or (2) a 
Change Order or Construction Change Directive has been issued authorizing the 
deviation. The Contractor shall not be relieved of responsibility for errors or omissions in 
Shop Drawings, Product Data, Samples or similar submittals by the Architect's approval 
thereof.

§ 3.12.10 The Contractor shall not be required to provide professional services which 
constitute the practice of architecture or engineering unless such services are specifically 
required by the Contract Documents for a portion of the Work or unless the Contractor

construction means, methods, techniques, sequences and procedures. The Contractor 
shall not be required to provide professional services in violation of applicable law. If 
professional design services or certifications by a design professional related to systems, 
materials or equipment are specifically required of the Contractor by the Contract 
Documents, the Owner and the Architect will specify all performance and design criteria 
that such services must satisfy. The Contractor shall cause such services or certifications 
to be provided by a properly licensed design professional, whose signature and seal shall 
appear on all drawings, calculations, specifications, certifications, Shop Drawings and 
other submittals prepared by such professional, and who shall provide evidence to the

other professional liability coverage prior to commencing design work. Shop Drawings 
and other submittals related to the Work designed or certified by such professional, if 
prepared by others, shall bear such professional's written approval when submitted to the 
Architect. The Owner and the Architect shall be entitled to rely upon the adequacy, 
accuracy and completeness of the services, certifications or approvals performed by such 
design professionals, provided the Owner and Architect have specified to the Contractor 
all performance and design criteria that such services must satisfy. Pursuant to this 
Subparagraph 3.12.10, the Architect will review, approve or take other appropriate action 
on submittals only for the limited purpose of checking for conformance with information 
given and the design concept expressed in the Contract Documents. The Contractor shall 
not be responsible for the adequacy of the performance or design criteria required by the 
Contract Documents. 
 
§ 3.13 USE OF SITE 
§ 3.13.1  The right of possession of the premises and the improvements made thereon by 
the Contractor shall remain at all times with the Owner. The Contractor’s right to entry 
and use thereof arises solely from the permission granted by the Owner under the 
Contract Documents. The Contractor shall confine his equipment, the storage of materials 
and the operations of his workmen to limits indicated by law, ordinances, the Contract 
Documents and permits and/or directions of the Architect and Owner and shall not 
unreasonably encumber the premises with his materials. 
 
§ 3.13.2 Only materials and equipment that are to be used directly in the Work shall be 
brought to and stored on the Project site by the Contractor. After equipment is no longer 
required for the Work, it shall be reasonably promptly removed from the Project site. 
Protection of construction materials and equipment stored at the Project site from 
weather, theft, damage, and all other adversity is the responsibility of the Contractor.

 
However, Contractor has the right to request reimbursement for such damages to the 
extent of coverage under Owner’s Builder’s Risk Insurance, (unless otherwise purchased

the Work and all adjacent areas. The Work shall be performed, to the fullest extent

conditions. 
 
§ 3.13.3 Without limitation of any other provision of the Contract Documents, the 
Contractor shall refrain from interfering with the occupancy or beneficial use of any areas 
and buildings adjacent to the site of the Work. 
 
§ 3.14  CUTTING AND PATCHING 
§ 3.14.1 The Contractor shall be responsible for cutting, fitting or patching required to 
complete the Work or to make its parts fit together properly. 
 
§ 3.14.2 The Contractor shall not damage or endanger a portion of the Work or fully or 
partially completed construction of the Owner or separate contractors by cutting, patching 
or otherwise altering such construction, or by excavation. The Contractor shall not cut or 
otherwise alter such construction by the Owner or a separate contractor except with 
written consent of the Owner and of such separate contractor; such consent shall not be 
unreasonably withheld. The Contractor shall not unreasonably withhold from the Owner 
or a separate contractor the Contractor's consent to cutting or otherwise altering the 
Work.    
 
§ 3.15 CLEANING UP 
§ 3.15.1 The Contractor shall keep the premises and surrounding area free from 
accumulation of waste materials or rubbish caused by operations under the Contract 
during the course of its Work. At completion of the Work, the Contractor shall promptly 
remove from and about the Project waste materials, rubbish, the Contractor's tools, 
construction equipment, machinery and surplus materials. 
 
§ 3.15.2 If the Contractor fails to clean up as provided in the Contract Documents, the 
Owner may do so and the cost thereof shall be charged to the Contractor. 
 
§ 3.16 ACCESS TO WORK 
§ 3.16.1 The Contractor shall provide the Owner and Architect access to the Work in 
preparation and progress wherever located.
